Aivazovsky's signature in Armenian on oil painting from 1899</div>

<p><b>Ivan Konstantinovich Aivazovsky</b> (<a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a>: <span lang="ru">ÐÐ²Ð°ÌÐ½ ÐÐ¾Ð½ÑÑÐ°Ð½ÑÐ¸ÌÐ½Ð¾Ð²Ð¸Ñ ÐÐ¹Ð²Ð°Ð·Ð¾ÌÐ²ÑÐºÐ¸Ð¹</span>; 29 July 1817Â â 2 May 1900) was a Russian <a href="/wiki/Romanticism" title="Romanticism">Romantic</a> <a href="/wiki/Painting" title="Painting">painter</a> who is considered one of the greatest masters of <a href="/wiki/Marine_art" title="Marine art">marine art</a>. Baptized as <b>Hovhannes Aivazian</b>, Aivazovsky was born into an <a href="/wiki/Armenians" title="Armenians">Armenian</a> family in the <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea" title="Black Sea">Black Sea</a> port of <a href="/wiki/Feodosia" title="Feodosia">Feodosia</a> in <a href="/wiki/Crimea" title="Crimea">Crimea</a> and was mostly based there.</p>
<p>Following his education at the <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Academy_of_Arts" title="Imperial Academy of Arts">Imperial Academy of Arts</a> in <a href="/wiki/Saint_Petersburg" title="Saint Petersburg">Saint Petersburg</a>, Aivazovsky traveled to Europe and lived briefly in <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a> in the early 1840s. He then returned to Russia and was appointed the main painter of the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Navy" title="Russian Navy">Russian Navy</a>. Aivazovsky had close ties with the military and political elite of the Russian Empire and often attended military maneuvers. He was sponsored by the state and was well-regarded during his lifetime. The saying "worthy of Aivazovsky's brush", popularized by <a href="/wiki/Anton_Chekhov" title="Anton Chekhov">Anton Chekhov</a>, was used in Russia for describing something lovely.</p>
<p>One of the most prominent <a href="/wiki/List_of_Russian_artists" title="List of Russian artists">Russian artists</a> of his time, Aivazovsky was also popular outside Russia. He held numerous <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Solo_exhibition" title="Solo exhibition">solo exhibitions</a> in Europe and the United States. During his almost 60-year career, he created around 6,000 paintings, making him one of the most prolific artists of his time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeek2012178_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeek2012178-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lang_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lang-4">[4]</a></sup> The vast majority of his works are <a href="/wiki/Seascape" title="Seascape">seascapes</a>, but he often depicted battle scenes, Armenian themes, and portraiture. Most of Aivazovsky's works are kept in Russian, <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukrainian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Armenia" title="Armenia">Armenian</a> museums as well as private collections.</p>
<p></p>

</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Background">Background</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ivan_Aivazovsky&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Background">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Ivan Aivazovsky was born on 17 July (29 in <a href="/wiki/Adoption_of_the_Gregorian_calendar#Adoption_in_Eastern_Europe" title="Adoption of the Gregorian calendar">New Style</a>) 1817 in the city of <a href="/wiki/Feodosia" title="Feodosia">Feodosia</a> (Theodosia), <a href="/wiki/Crimea" title="Crimea">Crimea</a>, Russian Empire.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ghazarian_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ghazarian-6">[6]</a></sup> In the baptismal records of the local St. Sargis <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Apostolic_Church" title="Armenian Apostolic Church">Armenian Apostolic</a> Church, Aivazovsky was listed as <i>Hovhannes, son of Gevorg Aivazian</i> (<a href="/wiki/Armenian_language" title="Armenian language">Armenian</a>: <span lang="hy">Ô³Õ§Õ¸ÖÕ£ Ô±ÕµÕ¾Õ¡Õ¦Õ¥Õ¡Õ¶Õ« Õ¸ÖÕ¤Õ« ÕÖÕ°Õ¡Õ¶Õ¶Õ¥Õ½Õ¶</span>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarutiunian196589_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarutiunian196589-7">[7]</a></sup> During his study at the <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Academy_of_Arts" title="Imperial Academy of Arts">Imperial Academy of Arts</a>, he was known in Russian as Ivan Gaivazovsky (ÐÐ²Ð°Ð½Ñ ÐÐ°Ð¹Ð²Ð°Ð·Ð¾Ð²ÑÐºÑÐ¹ in the pre-1918 spelling).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> He became known as Aivazovsky since <abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;">â1840</span>, while in Italy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarutiunian196593_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarutiunian196593-9">[9]</a></sup> He signed a 1844 letter with the <a href="/wiki/Italianization" title="Italianization">italianized</a> version of his name: Giovani Aivazovsky.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<p>His father, Konstantin, (<abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;">â1765</span>â1840),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMikaelian199169_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMikaelian199169-11">[11]</a></sup> was an Armenian merchant from the <a href="/wiki/Polish%E2%80%93Lithuanian_Commonwealth" title="PolishâLithuanian Commonwealth">Polish</a> region of <a href="/wiki/Galicia_(Eastern_Europe)" title="Galicia (Eastern Europe)">Galicia</a>. His family had migrated to Europe from <a href="/wiki/Western_Armenia" title="Western Armenia">Western Armenia</a> in the 18th century. After numerous familial conflicts, Konstantin left Galicia for <a href="/wiki/Moldavia" title="Moldavia">Moldavia</a>, later moving to <a href="/wiki/Bukovina" title="Bukovina">Bukovina</a>, before settling in Feodosia in the early 1800s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESarkssian196325_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESarkssian196325-12">[12]</a></sup> He was initially known as Gevorg Aivazian (Haivazian or Haivazi), but he changed his last name to Gaivazovsky by adding the Polish "<a href="/wiki/Polish_name#Suffix_-ski.2F-ska" title="Polish name">-sky</a>". Aivazovsky's mother, Ripsime, was a Feodosia Armenian. The couple had five childrenâthree daughters and two sons.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESarkssian196325_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESarkssian196325-12">[12]</a></sup> Aivazovsky's elder brother, <a href="/wiki/Gabriel_Aivazovsky" title="Gabriel Aivazovsky">Gabriel</a>, was a prominent historian and an Armenian Apostolic archbishop.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Aivazovsky_Sternberg_Italian.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1000" data-file-width="749" height="294" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Aivazovsky_Sternberg_Italian.jpg/220px-Aivazovsky_Sternberg_Italian.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Aivazovsky_Sternberg_Italian.jpg/330px-Aivazovsky_Sternberg_Italian.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Aivazovsky_Sternberg_Italian.jpg/440px-Aivazovsky_Sternberg_Italian.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Aivazovsky_Sternberg_Italian.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Aivazovsky in Italian costume, by <a class="extiw" href="https://ru.wikipedia.org/wiki/%D0%A8%D1%82%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%BD%D0%B1%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B3,_%D0%92%D0%B0%D1%81%D0%B8%D0%BB%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D0%98%D0%B2%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B8%D1%87" title="ru:Ð¨ÑÐµÑÐ½Ð±ÐµÑÐ³, ÐÐ°ÑÐ¸Ð»Ð¸Ð¹ ÐÐ²Ð°Ð½Ð¾Ð²Ð¸Ñ">Vasily Sternberg</a>, 1842</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ivan_Aivazovsky&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The young Aivazovsky received parochial education at Feodosia's St. Sargis Armenian Church.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMikaelian199159_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMikaelian199159-15">[15]</a></sup> He was taught drawing by Jacob Koch, a local architect. Aivazovsky moved to <a href="/wiki/Simferopol" title="Simferopol">Simferopol</a> with <a href="/wiki/Taurida_Governorate" title="Taurida Governorate">Taurida Governor</a> Alexander Kaznacheyev's family in 1830 and attended the city's <a href="/wiki/Simferopol_gymnasium_%E2%84%961" title="Simferopol gymnasium â1">Russian gymnasium</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> In 1833, Aivazovsky arrived in the Russian capital, <a href="/wiki/Saint_Petersburg" title="Saint Petersburg">Saint Petersburg</a>, to study at the Imperial Academy of Arts in <a href="/wiki/Maxim_Vorobiev" title="Maxim Vorobiev">Maxim Vorobiev</a>'s landscape class. In 1835, he was awarded with a silver medal and appointed assistant to the French painter Philippe Tanneur (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philippe_Tanneur" title="fr:Philippe Tanneur">fr</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tretyakovgallery_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-tretyakovgallery-17">[17]</a></sup> In September 1836, Aivazovsky met Russia's national poet <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Pushkin" title="Alexander Pushkin">Alexander Pushkin</a> during the latter's visit to the Academy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> In 1837, Aivazovsky joined the <a href="/wiki/Military_art" title="Military art">battle-painting</a> class of <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Sauerweid" title="Alexander Sauerweid">Alexander Sauerweid</a> and participated in <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Fleet" title="Baltic Fleet">Baltic Fleet</a> exercises in the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Finland" title="Gulf of Finland">Gulf of Finland</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RusArtNet_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-RusArtNet-20">[20]</a></sup> In October 1837, he graduated from the Imperial Academy of Arts with a gold medal, two years earlier than intended.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBolton2010140_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBolton2010140-21">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMikaelian199159_15-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMikaelian199159-15">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeek2012178_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeek2012178-3">[3]</a></sup> Aivazovsky returned to Feodosia in 1838 and spent two years in his native Crimea.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESarkssian196325_12-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESarkssian196325-12">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RusArtNet_20-1"><a href="#cite_note-RusArtNet-20">[20]</a></sup> In 1839, he took part in military exercises in the shores of Crimea, where he met Russian admirals <a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Lazarev" title="Mikhail Lazarev">Mikhail Lazarev</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pavel_Nakhimov" title="Pavel Nakhimov">Pavel Nakhimov</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vladimir_Alexeyevich_Kornilov" title="Vladimir Alexeyevich Kornilov">Vladimir Kornilov</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ghazarian_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-Ghazarian-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBolton2010141_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBolton2010141-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="First_visit_to_Europe">First visit to Europe</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ivan_Aivazovsky&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: First visit to Europe">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Portrait_of_Ivan_Konstantinovich_Aivazovsky_1841.png"><img alt="Alexey Tyranov's Portrait of Aivazovsky from 1841" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1174" data-file-width="880" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Portrait_of_Ivan_Konstantinovich_Aivazovsky_1841.png/170px-Portrait_of_Ivan_Konstantinovich_Aivazovsky_1841.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Portrait_of_Ivan_Konstantinovich_Aivazovsky_1841.png/255px-Portrait_of_Ivan_Konstantinovich_Aivazovsky_1841.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Portrait_of_Ivan_Konstantinovich_Aivazovsky_1841.png/340px-Portrait_of_Ivan_Konstantinovich_Aivazovsky_1841.png 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Portrait_of_Ivan_Konstantinovich_Aivazovsky_1841.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Portrait of Aivazovsky by <a href="/wiki/Alexey_Tyranov" title="Alexey Tyranov">Alexey Tyranov</a>, 1841</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1840, Aivazovsky was sent by the Imperial Academy of Arts to study in Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBolton2010140_21-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBolton2010140-21">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RusArtNet_20-2"><a href="#cite_note-RusArtNet-20">[20]</a></sup> He first traveled to <a href="/wiki/Venice" title="Venice">Venice</a> via <a href="/wiki/Berlin" title="Berlin">Berlin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">Vienna</a> and visited <a href="/wiki/San_Lazzaro_degli_Armeni" title="San Lazzaro degli Armeni">San Lazzaro degli Armeni</a>, where an important <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Armenian_Catholic" title="Armenian Catholic">Armenian Catholic</a> congregation was located and his brother Gabriel lived at the time. Aivazovsky studied Armenian manuscripts and became familiar with Armenian art.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Khachatrian_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-Khachatrian-23">[23]</a></sup> He met Russian novelist <a href="/wiki/Nikolai_Gogol" title="Nikolai Gogol">Nikolai Gogol</a> in Venice. He then headed to <a href="/wiki/Florence" title="Florence">Florence</a>, <a href="/wiki/Amalfi" title="Amalfi">Amalfi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sorrento" title="Sorrento">Sorrento</a>. In Florence, he met painter <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Andreyevich_Ivanov" title="Alexander Andreyevich Ivanov">Alexander Ivanov</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RusArtNet_20-3"><a href="#cite_note-RusArtNet-20">[20]</a></sup> He remained in <a href="/wiki/Naples" title="Naples">Naples</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rome" title="Rome">Rome</a> between 1840 and 1842. Aivazovsky was heavily influenced by Italian art and their museums became the "second academy" for him.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Khachatrian_23-1"><a href="#cite_note-Khachatrian-23">[23]</a></sup> According to Rogachevsky the news of successful exhibitions in Italy reached Russia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeek2012178_3-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeek2012178-3">[3]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Pope_Gregory_XVI" title="Pope Gregory XVI">Pope Gregory XVI</a> awarded him with a golden medal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rogachevsky_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rogachevsky-24">[24]</a></sup> He then visited Switzerland, Germany, the Netherlands and Britain, where he met English painter <a href="/wiki/J._M._W._Turner" title="J. M. W. Turner">J. M. W. Turner</a> who, "was so struck by Aivazovsky's picture <i>The Bay of Naples on a Moonlit Night</i> that he dedicated a rhymed eulogy in Italian to Aivazovsky."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBolton2010141_22-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBolton2010141-22">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RusArtNet_20-4"><a href="#cite_note-RusArtNet-20">[20]</a></sup> In an international exhibition at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Louvre" title="The Louvre">the Louvre</a>, he was the only representative from Russia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Khachatrian_23-2"><a href="#cite_note-Khachatrian-23">[23]</a></sup> In France, he received a gold medal from the <a href="/wiki/Acad%C3%A9mie_royale_de_peinture_et_de_sculpture" title="AcadÃ©mie royale de peinture et de sculpture">AcadÃ©mie royale de peinture et de sculpture</a>. He then returned to Naples via Marseille and again visited Britain, Portugal, Spain and Malta in 1843. Aivazovsky was admired throughout Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBolton2010141_22-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBolton2010141-22">[22]</a></sup> He returned to Russia via Paris and Amsterdam in 1844.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBolton2010141_22-3"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBolton2010141-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Return_to_Russia_and_first_marriage">Return to Russia and first marriage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ivan_Aivazovsky&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Return to Russia and first marriage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Aivazovsky_wife_and_daughters.png"><img alt="photograph of Aivazovsky with his first wife, Julia, and their four daughters" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="497" data-file-width="427" height="233" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Aivazovsky_wife_and_daughters.png/200px-Aivazovsky_wife_and_daughters.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Aivazovsky_wife_and_daughters.png/300px-Aivazovsky_wife_and_daughters.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Aivazovsky_wife_and_daughters.png/400px-Aivazovsky_wife_and_daughters.png 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Aivazovsky_wife_and_daughters.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Aivazovsky with his first wife, Julia, and their four daughters</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Upon his return to Russia, Aivazovsky was made an academician of the Imperial Academy of Arts and was appointed the "official artist of the Russian Navy to paint seascapes, coastal scenes and naval battles."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tretyakovgallery_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-tretyakovgallery-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RusArtNet_20-5"><a href="#cite_note-RusArtNet-20">[20]</a></sup> In 1845, Aivazovsky traveled to the <a href="/wiki/Aegean_Sea" title="Aegean Sea">Aegean Sea</a> with <a href="/wiki/Grand_Duke_Konstantin_Nikolayevich_of_Russia" title="Grand Duke Konstantin Nikolayevich of Russia">Duke Konstantin Nikolayevich</a> and visited the Ottoman capital, <a href="/wiki/Constantinople" title="Constantinople">Constantinople</a>, and the Greek islands of <a href="/wiki/Patmos" title="Patmos">Patmos</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rhodes" title="Rhodes">Rhodes</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RusArtNet_20-6"><a href="#cite_note-RusArtNet-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1845, Aivazovsky settled in his hometown of Feodosia, where he built a house and studio.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ghazarian_6-2"><a href="#cite_note-Ghazarian-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RusArtNet_20-7"><a href="#cite_note-RusArtNet-20">[20]</a></sup> He isolated himself from the outside world, keeping a small circle of friends and relatives.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Khachatrian_23-3"><a href="#cite_note-Khachatrian-23">[23]</a></sup> Yet the solitude played a negative role in his art career. By the mid-nineteenth century, Russian art was moving from <a href="/wiki/Romanticism" title="Romanticism">Romanticism</a> towards a distinct Russian style of <a href="/wiki/Realism_(arts)" title="Realism (arts)">Realism</a>, while Aivazovsky continued to paint Romantic seascapes and attracted heavy criticism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Khachatrian_23-4"><a href="#cite_note-Khachatrian-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1845 and 1846, Aivazovsky attended the maneuvers of the <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea_Fleet" title="Black Sea Fleet">Black Sea Fleet</a> and the Baltic Fleet at <a href="/wiki/Petergof" title="Petergof">Petergof</a>, near the <a href="/wiki/Peterhof_Palace" title="Peterhof Palace">imperial palace</a>. In 1847, he was given the title of professor of seascape painting by the Imperial Academy of Arts and elevated to the rank of nobility. In the same year, he was elected to the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Netherlands_Academy_of_Arts_and_Sciences" title="Royal Netherlands Academy of Arts and Sciences">Royal Netherlands Academy of Arts and Sciences</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RusArtNet_20-8"><a href="#cite_note-RusArtNet-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1848, Aivazovsky married Julia Graves, an English governess. They had four daughters: Elena (1849), Maria (1851), Alexandra (1852) and Joanne (1858). They separated in 1860 and divorced in 1877 with permission from the <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Apostolic_Church" title="Armenian Apostolic Church">Armenian Church</a>, since Graves was a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lutheran" title="Lutheran">Lutheran</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RusArtNet_20-9"><a href="#cite_note-RusArtNet-20">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMikaelian199163_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMikaelian199163-25">[25]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rise_to_prominence">Rise to prominence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ivan_Aivazovsky&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Rise to prominence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ayvaz_sredy_voln.jpg"><img alt="painting of whitecaps on the sea" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1815" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Ayvaz_sredy_voln.jpg/220px-Ayvaz_sredy_voln.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Ayvaz_sredy_voln.jpg/330px-Ayvaz_sredy_voln.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Ayvaz_sredy_voln.jpg/440px-Ayvaz_sredy_voln.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ayvaz_sredy_voln.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The vast majority of his works depict the sea. Pictured is a 1898 painting titled <i>Among the Waves</i>, Aivazovsky National Art Gallery, Feodosia</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1851, traveling with the Russian emperor <a href="/wiki/Nicholas_I_of_Russia" title="Nicholas I of Russia">Nicholas I</a>, Aivazovsky sailed to <a href="/wiki/Sevastopol" title="Sevastopol">Sevastopol</a> to participate in military maneuvers. His archaeological excavations near Feodosia lead to his election as a full member of the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Geographical_Society" title="Russian Geographical Society">Russian Geographical Society</a> in 1853. In that year, the <a href="/wiki/Crimean_War" title="Crimean War">Crimean War</a> erupted between Russia and the Ottoman Empire, and he was evacuated to <a href="/wiki/Kharkiv" title="Kharkiv">Kharkiv</a>. While safe, he returned to the besieged fortress of Sevastopol to paint battle scenes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rogachevsky_24-1"><a href="#cite_note-Rogachevsky-24">[24]</a></sup> His work was exhibited in Sevastopol while it was under Ottoman siege.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rogachevsky_24-2"><a href="#cite_note-Rogachevsky-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<p>Between 1856 and 1857, Aivazovsky worked in Paris and became the first Russian<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gomtsyan_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gomtsyan-26">[26]</a></sup> (and the first non-French) artist to receive the <a href="/wiki/Legion_of_Honour" title="Legion of Honour">Legion of Honour</a>. In 1857, Aivazovsky visited Constantinople and was awarded the <a href="/wiki/Order_of_the_Medjidie" title="Order of the Medjidie">Order of the Medjidie</a>. In the same year he was elected an honorary member of the Moscow Art Society. He was awarded the Greek <a href="/wiki/Order_of_the_Redeemer" title="Order of the Redeemer">Order of the Redeemer</a> in 1859 and the Russian <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Order_of_St._Vladimir" title="Order of St. Vladimir">Order of St. Vladimir</a> in 1865.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rogachevsky_24-3"><a href="#cite_note-Rogachevsky-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<p>Aivazovsky opened an art studio in Feodosia in 1865 and was awarded a salary by the Imperial Academy of Arts the same year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RusArtNet_20-10"><a href="#cite_note-RusArtNet-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Aivazovsky_1870_photo.jpg"><img alt="A photograph of Aivazovsky, facing left with whiskers from 1870" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="433" height="236" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Aivazovsky_1870_photo.jpg/170px-Aivazovsky_1870_photo.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Aivazovsky_1870_photo.jpg/255px-Aivazovsky_1870_photo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Aivazovsky_1870_photo.jpg/340px-Aivazovsky_1870_photo.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Aivazovsky_1870_photo.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A photograph of Aivazovsky, 1870</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span id="Travels_and_accolades:_1860sâ1880s"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Travels_and_accolades:_1860s.E2.80.931880s">Travels and accolades: 1860sâ1880s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ivan_Aivazovsky&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Travels and accolades: 1860sâ1880s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the 1860s, the artist produced several paintings inspired by Greek nationalism and the <a href="/wiki/Italian_unification" title="Italian unification">Italian unification</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ghazarian_6-3"><a href="#cite_note-Ghazarian-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rogachevsky_24-4"><a href="#cite_note-Rogachevsky-24">[24]</a></sup> In 1868, he once again visited Constantinople and produced a series of works about the Greek resistance to the Turks, during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cretan_Revolt_(1866%E2%80%9369)" title="Cretan Revolt (1866â69)">Great Cretan Revolution</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RusArtNet_20-11"><a href="#cite_note-RusArtNet-20">[20]</a></sup> In 1868, Aivazovsky traveled in the <a href="/wiki/Caucasus" title="Caucasus">Caucasus</a> and visited the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Armenia" title="Russian Armenia">Russian part of Armenia</a> for the first time. He painted several mountainous landscapes and in 1869 held an exhibition in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tiflis" title="Tiflis">Tiflis</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ghazarian_6-4"><a href="#cite_note-Ghazarian-6">[6]</a></sup> Later in the year, he made a trip to Egypt and took part in the opening ceremony of the <a href="/wiki/Suez_Canal" title="Suez Canal">Suez Canal</a>. He became the "first artist to paint the Suez Canal, thus marking an epoch-making event in the history of Europe, Africa and Asia."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rogachevsky_24-5"><a href="#cite_note-Rogachevsky-24">[24]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1870, Aivazovsky was made an <a href="/wiki/Table_of_Ranks" title="Table of Ranks">Actual Civil Councilor</a>, the fourth highest civil rank in Russia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RusArtNet_20-12"><a href="#cite_note-RusArtNet-20">[20]</a></sup> In 1871, he initiated the construction of the archaeological museum in Feodosia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rogachevsky_24-6"><a href="#cite_note-Rogachevsky-24">[24]</a></sup> In 1872, he traveled to Nice and Florence to exhibit his paintings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rogachevsky_24-7"><a href="#cite_note-Rogachevsky-24">[24]</a></sup> In 1874, the <a href="/wiki/Accademia_di_Belle_Arti_di_Firenze" title="Accademia di Belle Arti di Firenze">Accademia di Belle Arti di Firenze</a> (Florence Academy of Fine Art) asked him for a self-portrait to be hung in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Uffizi_Gallery" title="Uffizi Gallery">Uffizi Gallery</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rutgers_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-rutgers-28">[28]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> The same year, Aivazovsky was invited to Constantinople by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sultan_Abd%C3%BClaziz" title="Sultan AbdÃ¼laziz">Sultan AbdÃ¼laziz</a> who subsequently bestowed upon him the Turkish <a href="/wiki/Order_of_Osmanieh" title="Order of Osmanieh">Order of Osmanieh</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RusArtNet_20-13"><a href="#cite_note-RusArtNet-20">[20]</a></sup> In 1876, he was made a member of the Academy of Arts in Florence and became the second Russian artist (after <a href="/wiki/Orest_Kiprensky" title="Orest Kiprensky">Orest Kiprensky</a>) to paint a self-portrait for the <a href="/wiki/Palazzo_Pitti" title="Palazzo Pitti">Palazzo Pitti</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Khachatrian_23-5"><a href="#cite_note-Khachatrian-23">[23]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rogachevsky_24-8"><a href="#cite_note-Rogachevsky-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<p>Aivazovsky was elected an honorary member of <a href="/wiki/Stuttgart" title="Stuttgart">Stuttgart</a>'s Royal Academy of Fine Arts (<a class="extiw" href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Staatliche_Akademie_der_Bildenden_K%C3%BCnste_Stuttgart" title="de:Staatliche Akademie der Bildenden KÃ¼nste Stuttgart">de</a>) in 1878. He made a trip to the Netherlands and France, staying briefly in <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt" title="Frankfurt">Frankfurt</a> until 1879. He then visited <a href="/wiki/Munich" title="Munich">Munich</a> and traveled to <a href="/wiki/Genoa" title="Genoa">Genoa</a> and Venice "to collect material on the discovery of America by Christopher Columbus."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rogachevsky_24-9"><a href="#cite_note-Rogachevsky-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1880, Aivazovsky opened an art gallery in his Feodosia house; it became the third museum in the Russian Empire, after the <a href="/wiki/Hermitage_Museum" title="Hermitage Museum">Hermitage Museum</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Tretyakov_Gallery" title="Tretyakov Gallery">Tretyakov Gallery</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Khachatrian_23-6"><a href="#cite_note-Khachatrian-23">[23]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rogachevsky_24-10"><a href="#cite_note-Rogachevsky-24">[24]</a></sup> Aivazovsky held an 1881 exhibition at London's <a href="/wiki/Pall_Mall,_London" title="Pall Mall, London">Pall Mall</a>, attended by English painter <a href="/wiki/John_Everett_Millais" title="John Everett Millais">John Everett Millais</a> and <a href="/wiki/Edward_VII" title="Edward VII">Edward VII</a>, <a href="/wiki/Prince_of_Wales" title="Prince of Wales">Prince of Wales</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RusArtNet_20-14"><a href="#cite_note-RusArtNet-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Second_marriage_and_later_life">Second marriage and later life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ivan_Aivazovsky&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Second marriage and later life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tmulti tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:321px;max-width:321px">
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:152px;max-width:152px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Aivazovsky_by_Bolotov,_1876.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="1499" data-file-width="1182" height="190" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Aivazovsky_by_Bolotov%2C_1876.jpg/150px-Aivazovsky_by_Bolotov%2C_1876.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Aivazovsky_by_Bolotov%2C_1876.jpg/225px-Aivazovsky_by_Bolotov%2C_1876.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Aivazovsky_by_Bolotov%2C_1876.jpg/300px-Aivazovsky_by_Bolotov%2C_1876.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">
<center>Portrait of Aivazovsky by Dmitry Bolotov (1876)</center>
</div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:165px;max-width:165px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Aivazovsky_-_Portret_of_wife,_Anna_Burnazyan-Sarkisova.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="700" data-file-width="601" height="190" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Aivazovsky_-_Portret_of_wife%2C_Anna_Burnazyan-Sarkisova.jpg/163px-Aivazovsky_-_Portret_of_wife%2C_Anna_Burnazyan-Sarkisova.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Aivazovsky_-_Portret_of_wife%2C_Anna_Burnazyan-Sarkisova.jpg/245px-Aivazovsky_-_Portret_of_wife%2C_Anna_Burnazyan-Sarkisova.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Aivazovsky_-_Portret_of_wife%2C_Anna_Burnazyan-Sarkisova.jpg/326px-Aivazovsky_-_Portret_of_wife%2C_Anna_Burnazyan-Sarkisova.jpg 2x" width="163"/></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">
<center>Aivazovsky's painting of his second wife Anna Burnazian (1882)</center>
</div>
</div>
<div style="clear:left"></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Aivazovsky's second wife, Anna Burnazian, was a young Armenian widow 40 years his junior.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Obukhovska_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-Obukhovska-30">[30]</a></sup> Aivazovsky said that by marrying her in 1882, he "became closer to [his] nation", referring to the Armenian people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMikaelian199163_25-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMikaelian199163-25">[25]</a></sup> In 1882, Aivazovsky visited Moscow and St Petersburg and then toured the countryside of Russia by traveling along the <a href="/wiki/Volga_River" title="Volga River">Volga River</a> in 1884.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RusArtNet_20-15"><a href="#cite_note-RusArtNet-20">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rogachevsky_24-11"><a href="#cite_note-Rogachevsky-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1885, he was promoted to the rank of <a href="/wiki/Table_of_Ranks" title="Table of Ranks">Privy Councilor</a>. The next year, the 50th anniversary of his creative labors, was celebrated with an exhibition in St Petersburg, and an honorary membership in the Imperial Academy of Fine Arts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tretyakovgallery_17-2"><a href="#cite_note-tretyakovgallery-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rogachevsky_24-12"><a href="#cite_note-Rogachevsky-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<p>After meeting Aivazovsky in person, <a href="/wiki/Anton_Chekhov" title="Anton Chekhov">Anton Chekhov</a> wrote a letter to his wife on 22 July 1888 describing him as follows:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chekhov_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-Chekhov-31">[31]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup></p>
<blockquote class="toccolours" style="float:none; display:table;">
<div style="padding: 10px 15px 10px 15px;">Aivazovsky himself is a hale and hearty old man of about seventy-five, looking like an insignificant Armenian and an bishop; he is full of a sense of his own importance, has soft hands and shakes your hand like a general. He's not very bright, but he is a complex personality, worthy of a further study. In him alone there are combined a general, a bishop, an artist, an Armenian, an naive old peasant, and an Othello.</div>
</blockquote>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:277px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%D0%94%D0%BE%D0%BC,_%D0%B2_%D0%BA%D0%BE%D1%82%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%BC_%D0%B6%D0%B8%D0%BB_%D1%85%D1%83%D0%B4%D0%BE%D0%B6%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BA_%D0%98._%D0%9A._%D0%90%D0%B9%D0%B2%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%BE%D0%B2%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9_1845-1892.JPG"><img alt="The house in Feodosia, where Aivazovsky lived between 1845 and 1892 now an Aivazovsky National Art Gallery" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1632" data-file-width="2464" height="182" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/%D0%94%D0%BE%D0%BC%2C_%D0%B2_%D0%BA%D0%BE%D1%82%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%BC_%D0%B6%D0%B8%D0%BB_%D1%85%D1%83%D0%B4%D0%BE%D0%B6%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BA_%D0%98._%D0%9A._%D0%90%D0%B9%D0%B2%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%BE%D0%B2%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9_1845-1892.JPG/275px-%D0%94%D0%BE%D0%BC%2C_%D0%B2_%D0%BA%D0%BE%D1%82%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%BC_%D0%B6%D0%B8%D0%BB_%D1%85%D1%83%D0%B4%D0%BE%D0%B6%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BA_%D0%98._%D0%9A._%D0%90%D0%B9%D0%B2%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%BE%D0%B2%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9_1845-1892.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/%D0%94%D0%BE%D0%BC%2C_%D0%B2_%D0%BA%D0%BE%D1%82%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%BC_%D0%B6%D0%B8%D0%BB_%D1%85%D1%83%D0%B4%D0%BE%D0%B6%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BA_%D0%98._%D0%9A._%D0%90%D0%B9%D0%B2%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%BE%D0%B2%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9_1845-1892.JPG/413px-%D0%94%D0%BE%D0%BC%2C_%D0%B2_%D0%BA%D0%BE%D1%82%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%BC_%D0%B6%D0%B8%D0%BB_%D1%85%D1%83%D0%B4%D0%BE%D0%B6%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BA_%D0%98._%D0%9A._%D0%90%D0%B9%D0%B2%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%BE%D0%B2%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9_1845-1892.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/%D0%94%D0%BE%D0%BC%2C_%D0%B2_%D0%BA%D0%BE%D1%82%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%BC_%D0%B6%D0%B8%D0%BB_%D1%85%D1%83%D0%B4%D0%BE%D0%B6%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BA_%D0%98._%D0%9A._%D0%90%D0%B9%D0%B2%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%BE%D0%B2%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9_1845-1892.JPG/550px-%D0%94%D0%BE%D0%BC%2C_%D0%B2_%D0%BA%D0%BE%D1%82%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%BC_%D0%B6%D0%B8%D0%BB_%D1%85%D1%83%D0%B4%D0%BE%D0%B6%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BA_%D0%98._%D0%9A._%D0%90%D0%B9%D0%B2%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%BE%D0%B2%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9_1845-1892.JPG 2x" width="275"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%D0%94%D0%BE%D0%BC,_%D0%B2_%D0%BA%D0%BE%D1%82%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%BC_%D0%B6%D0%B8%D0%BB_%D1%85%D1%83%D0%B4%D0%BE%D0%B6%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BA_%D0%98._%D0%9A._%D0%90%D0%B9%D0%B2%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%BE%D0%B2%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9_1845-1892.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The house in Feodosia, where Aivazovsky lived between 1845 and 1892. It is now an <a href="/wiki/Aivazovsky_National_Art_Gallery" title="Aivazovsky National Art Gallery">art gallery</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After traveling to Paris with his wife, in 1892 he made a trip to the United States, visiting <a href="/wiki/Niagara_Falls" title="Niagara Falls">Niagara Falls</a> in New York and Washington D.C.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rogachevsky_24-13"><a href="#cite_note-Rogachevsky-24">[24]</a></sup> In 1896, at 79, Aivazovsky was promoted to the rank of full privy councillor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RusArtNet_20-16"><a href="#cite_note-RusArtNet-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<p>Aivazovsky was deeply affected by the <a href="/wiki/Hamidian_massacres" title="Hamidian massacres">Hamidian massacres</a> that took place in the Armenian-inhabited areas of the Ottoman Empire between 1894 and 1896. He painted a number of works on the subject such as <i>The Expulsion of the Turkish Ship</i>, and <i>The Armenian Massacres at Trebizond</i>. He threw the medals given to him by the Ottoman Sultan into the sea and told the Turkish consul in Feodosia: "Tell your bloodthirsty master that I've thrown away all the medals given to me, here are their ribbons, send it to him and if he wants, he can throw them into the seas painted by me."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarutiunian196590.E2.80.9391_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarutiunian196590.E2.80.9391-33">[33]</a></sup> He created several painting on the events, such as <i>The Massacre of Armenians in Trebizond</i> (1895), <i>Lonely Ship</i>, <i>Night. Tragedy in the Sea of Marmara</i> (1897).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKoorghinian1967190_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKoorghinian1967190-34">[34]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESarkssian196331_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESarkssian196331-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:259px;max-width:259px">
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:257px;max-width:257px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ajwazowski_grob.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="2536" data-file-width="3748" height="173" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Ajwazowski_grob.jpg/255px-Ajwazowski_grob.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Ajwazowski_grob.jpg/383px-Ajwazowski_grob.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Ajwazowski_grob.jpg/510px-Ajwazowski_grob.jpg 2x" width="255"/></a></div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:257px;max-width:257px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Feodosiya_tomb_of_Ivan_Aivazovsky_IMG_2968_1725.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="1028" data-file-width="2524" height="104" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Feodosiya_tomb_of_Ivan_Aivazovsky_IMG_2968_1725.jpg/255px-Feodosiya_tomb_of_Ivan_Aivazovsky_IMG_2968_1725.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Feodosiya_tomb_of_Ivan_Aivazovsky_IMG_2968_1725.jpg/383px-Feodosiya_tomb_of_Ivan_Aivazovsky_IMG_2968_1725.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Feodosiya_tomb_of_Ivan_Aivazovsky_IMG_2968_1725.jpg/510px-Feodosiya_tomb_of_Ivan_Aivazovsky_IMG_2968_1725.jpg 2x" width="255"/></a></div>
</div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center;background-color:transparent">Tomb of Aivazovsky</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>He spent his final years in Feodosia. In the 1890s, thanks to his efforts a <a class="extiw" href="https://ru.wikipedia.org/wiki/%D0%A4%D0%B5%D0%BE%D0%B4%D0%BE%D1%81%D0%B8%D0%B9%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D0%BC%D0%BE%D1%80%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B9_%D1%82%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%B3%D0%BE%D0%B2%D1%8B%D0%B9_%D0%BF%D0%BE%D1%80%D1%82" title="ru:Ð¤ÐµÐ¾Ð´Ð¾ÑÐ¸Ð¹ÑÐºÐ¸Ð¹ Ð¼Ð¾ÑÑÐºÐ¾Ð¹ ÑÐ¾ÑÐ³Ð¾Ð²ÑÐ¹ Ð¿Ð¾ÑÑ">commercial port</a> was established in Feodosia and linked to the railway network of the Russian Empire.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Obukhovska_30-1"><a href="#cite_note-Obukhovska-30">[30]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Whitmore_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-Whitmore-36">[36]</a></sup> The railway station, opened in 1892, is now called <i><a class="extiw" href="https://ru.wikipedia.org/wiki/%D0%90%D0%B9%D0%B2%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%BE%D0%B2%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B0%D1%8F_(%D1%81%D1%82%D0%B0%D0%BD%D1%86%D0%B8%D1%8F)" title="ru:ÐÐ¹Ð²Ð°Ð·Ð¾Ð²ÑÐºÐ°Ñ (ÑÑÐ°Ð½ÑÐ¸Ñ)">Ayvazovskaya</a></i> and is one of the two stations within the city of Feodosia. Aivazovsky also supplied Feodosia with drinking water.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Death">Death</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ivan_Aivazovsky&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Death">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Aivazovsky died on 19 April (2 May in New Style) 1900 in Feodosia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rogachevsky_24-14"><a href="#cite_note-Rogachevsky-24">[24]</a></sup> In accordance with his wishes, he was buried at the courtyard of St. Sargis Armenian Church.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-artrenewal_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-artrenewal-39">[39]</a></sup> A white marble <a href="/wiki/Sarcophagus" title="Sarcophagus">sarcophagus</a> was made by Italian sculptor L. Biogiolli in 1901.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> A quote from <a href="/wiki/Movses_Khorenatsi" title="Movses Khorenatsi">Movses Khorenatsi</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/History_of_Armenia_(book)" title="History of Armenia (book)">History of Armenia</a></i> in <a href="/wiki/Classical_Armenian" title="Classical Armenian">Classical Armenian</a> is engraved on his tombstone: ÕÕ¡Õ°Õ¯Õ¡Õ¶Õ¡ÖÕ¸Ö Õ®Õ¶Õ¥Õ¡Õ¬ Õ¡Õ¶Õ´Õ¡Õ° Õ¦Õ«ÖÖÕ¶ ÕµÕ«Õ·Õ¡Õ¿Õ¡Õ¯ Õ¥Õ©Õ¸Õ² (<i>Mahkanatsu tsneal anmah ziurn yishatak yetogh</i>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gallery.am_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-gallery.am-41">[41]</a></sup> which translates: "He was born a mortal, left an immortal legacy"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-artrenewal_39-1"><a href="#cite_note-artrenewal-39">[39]</a></sup> or "Born as a mortal, left the immortal memory of himself".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Minasyan_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-Minasyan-42">[42]</a></sup> After his death, his wife Anna led a generally secluded life and died on July 25, 1944. She was buried next to Aivazovsky.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Obukhovska_30-2"><a href="#cite_note-Obukhovska-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Art">Art</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ivan_Aivazovsky&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Art">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:327px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hovhannes_Aivazovsky_-_The_Ninth_Wave_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg"><img alt="Aivazovsky painting The Ninth Wave from 1850" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3420" data-file-width="5090" height="218" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Hovhannes_Aivazovsky_-_The_Ninth_Wave_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/325px-Hovhannes_Aivazovsky_-_The_Ninth_Wave_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Hovhannes_Aivazovsky_-_The_Ninth_Wave_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/488px-Hovhannes_Aivazovsky_-_The_Ninth_Wave_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Hovhannes_Aivazovsky_-_The_Ninth_Wave_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/650px-Hovhannes_Aivazovsky_-_The_Ninth_Wave_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg 2x" width="325"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hovhannes_Aivazovsky_-_The_Ninth_Wave_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i><a href="/wiki/The_Ninth_Wave" title="The Ninth Wave">The Ninth Wave</a></i> (1850, <a href="/wiki/Russian_Museum" title="Russian Museum">Russian Museum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saint_Petersburg" title="Saint Petersburg">Saint Petersburg</a>) is considered Aivazovsky's most famous work.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>During his 60 year career, Aivazovsky produced around 6,000 paintings<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tretyakovgallery_17-3"><a href="#cite_note-tretyakovgallery-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rogachevsky_24-15"><a href="#cite_note-Rogachevsky-24">[24]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESarkssian196326_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESarkssian196326-46">[46]</a></sup> of, what one online art magazine describes, "very different valueÂ ... there are masterpieces and there are very timid works".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-athenaeum_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-athenaeum-47">[47]</a></sup> However, according to one count as many as 20,000 paintings are attributed to him.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> The vast majority of Aivazovsky's works depict the sea.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeek2012178.E2.80.93180_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeek2012178.E2.80.93180-49">[49]</a></sup> He rarely drew dry-landscapes and created only a handful of portraits.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-athenaeum_47-1"><a href="#cite_note-athenaeum-47">[47]</a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/Rosa_Newmarch" title="Rosa Newmarch">Rosa Newmarch</a> Aivazovsky "never painted his pictures from nature, always from memory, and far away from the seaboard."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENewmarch1917192_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENewmarch1917192-50">[50]</a></sup> Rogachevsky wrote that "His artistic memory was legendary. He was able to reproduce what he had seen only for a very short time, without even drawing preliminary sketches."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rogachevsky_24-16"><a href="#cite_note-Rogachevsky-24">[24]</a></sup> Bolton praised "his ability to convey the effect of moving water and of reflected sun and moonlight."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBolton2010140_21-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBolton2010140-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Exhibitions">Exhibitions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ivan_Aivazovsky&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Exhibitions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>He held 55 solo exhibitions (an unprecedented number)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rusmuseum.ru_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-rusmuseum.ru-51">[51]</a></sup> over the course of his career. Among the most notable were held in Rome, Naples and Venice (1841â42), Paris (1843, 1890), Amsterdam (1844), Moscow (1848, 1851, 1886), Sevastopol (1854), Tiflis (1868), Florence (1874), St. Petersburg (1875, 1877, 1886, 1891), Frankfurt (1879), Stuttgart (1879), London (1881), Berlin (1885, 1890), Warsaw (1885), Constantinople (1888), New York (1893), Chicago (1893), San Francisco (1893).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RusArtNet_20-17"><a href="#cite_note-RusArtNet-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<p>He also "contributed to the exhibitions of the Imperial Academy of Arts (1836â1900), <a href="/wiki/Salon_(Paris)" title="Salon (Paris)">Paris Salon</a> (1843, 1879), Society of Exhibitions of Works of Art (1876â83), Moscow Society of Lovers of the Arts (1880), Pan-Russian Exhibitions in Moscow (1882) and Nizhny Novgorod (1896), World Exhibitions in Paris (<a href="/wiki/Exposition_Universelle_(1855)" title="Exposition Universelle (1855)">1855</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/International_Exposition_(1867)" title="International Exposition (1867)">1867</a>, <a href="/wiki/Exposition_Universelle_(1878)" title="Exposition Universelle (1878)">1878</a>), <a href="/wiki/1862_International_Exhibition" title="1862 International Exhibition">London (1863)</a>, Munich (1879) and <a href="/wiki/World%27s_Columbian_Exposition" title="World's Columbian Exposition">Chicago (1893)</a> and the international exhibitions in <a href="/wiki/Centennial_Exposition" title="Centennial Exposition">Philadelphia (1876)</a>, Munich (1879) and <a href="/wiki/Great_Industrial_Exposition_of_Berlin" title="Great Industrial Exposition of Berlin">Berlin (1896)</a>."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RusArtNet_20-18"><a href="#cite_note-RusArtNet-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Stormy_sea_at_night.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="915" data-file-width="1100" height="250" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Stormy_sea_at_night.jpg/300px-Stormy_sea_at_night.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Stormy_sea_at_night.jpg/450px-Stormy_sea_at_night.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Stormy_sea_at_night.jpg/600px-Stormy_sea_at_night.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Stormy_sea_at_night.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i>Stormy Sea at Night</i>, 1849, <a href="/wiki/Pavlovsk_Palace" title="Pavlovsk Palace">Pavlovsk Palace</a>, Saint Petersburg</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Style">Style</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ivan_Aivazovsky&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Style">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>A primarily Romantic painter, Aivazovsky used some Realistic elements.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKoorghinian1967189_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKoorghinian1967189-52">[52]</a></sup> Leek argued that Aivazovsky remained faithful to Romanticism] throughout his life, "even though he oriented his work toward the Realist genre."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeek2012178_3-3"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeek2012178-3">[3]</a></sup> His early works are influenced by his Academy of Arts teachers Maxim Vorobiev and <a href="/wiki/Sylvester_Shchedrin" title="Sylvester Shchedrin">Sylvester Shchedrin</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tretyakovgallery_17-4"><a href="#cite_note-tretyakovgallery-17">[17]</a></sup> Classic painters like <a href="/wiki/Salvator_Rosa" title="Salvator Rosa">Salvator Rosa</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jacob_Isaacksz_van_Ruisdael" title="Jacob Isaacksz van Ruisdael">Jacob Isaacksz van Ruisdael</a> and <a href="/wiki/Claude_Lorrain" title="Claude Lorrain">Claude Lorrain</a> contributed to Aivazovsky's individual process and style.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ghazarian_6-5"><a href="#cite_note-Ghazarian-6">[6]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Karl_Bryullov" title="Karl Bryullov">Karl Bryullov</a>, best known for his <i><a href="/wiki/The_Last_Day_of_Pompeii" title="The Last Day of Pompeii">The Last Day of Pompeii</a></i>, "played an important part in stimulating Aivazovsky's own creative development," according to Bolton.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBolton2010140_21-3"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBolton2010140-21">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tretyakovgallery_17-5"><a href="#cite_note-tretyakovgallery-17">[17]</a></sup> Aivazovsky's best paintings in the 1840sâ1850s used a variety of colors and were both epic and romantic in theme.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ghazarian_6-6"><a href="#cite_note-Ghazarian-6">[6]</a></sup> Newmarch suggested that by the mid-19th century the romantic features in AivazovskyÂ's work became "increasingly pronounced."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-athenaeum_47-2"><a href="#cite_note-athenaeum-47">[47]</a></sup> She, like most scholars, considered his <i>Ninth Wave</i> his best piece of art and argued that it "seems to mark the transition between fantastic color of his earlier works, and the more truthful vision of the later years."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENewmarch1917191_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENewmarch1917191-53">[53]</a></sup> By the 1870s, his paintings were dominated by delicate colors; and in the last two decades of his life, Aivazovsky created a series of silver-toned seascapes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ghazarian_6-7"><a href="#cite_note-Ghazarian-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<p>The distinct transition in Russian art from Romanticism to Realism in the mid-nineteenth century left Aivazovsky, who would always retain a Romantic style, open to criticism. Proposed reasons for his unwillingness or inability to change began with his location; Feodosia was a remote town in the huge Russian empire, far from Moscow and Saint Petersburg. His mindset and worldview were similarly considered old-fashioned, and did not correspond to the developments in Russian art and culture.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Khachatrian_23-7"><a href="#cite_note-Khachatrian-23">[23]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Stasov" title="Vladimir Stasov">Vladimir Stasov</a> only accepted his early works, while <a href="/wiki/Alexandre_Benois" title="Alexandre Benois">Alexandre Benois</a> wrote in his <i>The History of Russian Painting in the 19th Century</i> that despite being Vorobiev's student, Aivazovsky stood apart from the general development of the Russian landscape school.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Khachatrian_23-8"><a href="#cite_note-Khachatrian-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<p>Aivazovsky's later work contained dramatic scenes and was usually done on a larger scale. He depicted "the romantic struggle between man and the elements in the form of the sea (<i>The Rainbow</i>, 1873), and so-called "blue marines" (<i>The Bay of Naples in Early Morning</i>, 1897, <i>Disaster</i>, 1898) and urban landscapes (<i>Moonlit Night on the Bosphorus</i>, 1894)."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tretyakovgallery_17-6"><a href="#cite_note-tretyakovgallery-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Works">Works</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ivan_Aivazovsky&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Works">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Landscapes">Landscapes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ivan_Aivazovsky&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Landscapes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional">

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Armenian_themes">Armenian themes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ivan_Aivazovsky&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Armenian themes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Aivazovsky's early works incorporated Armenian themes. The artist's longstanding wish to visit his ancestral homeland was fulfilled in 1868. During his visit to Russian (Eastern) Armenia (roughly corresponding to the modern <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Republic_of_Armenia" title="Republic of Armenia">Republic of Armenia</a>, as opposed to <a href="/wiki/Western_Armenia" title="Western Armenia">Western Armenia</a> under Ottoman rule), Aivazovsky created paintings of <a href="/wiki/Mount_Ararat" title="Mount Ararat">Mount Ararat</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ararat_plain" title="Ararat plain">Ararat plain</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Lake_Sevan" title="Lake Sevan">Lake Sevan</a>. Although Mt. Ararat has been depicted in paintings of many non-native artists (mostly European travelers), Aivazovsky became the first Armenian artist to illustrate the two-peaked biblical mountain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESarkssian196328_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESarkssian196328-54">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Khachatrian_23-9"><a href="#cite_note-Khachatrian-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<p>He resumed the creation of Armenian-related paintings in the 1880s: <i>Valley of Mount Ararat</i> (1882), <i>Ararat</i> (1887), <i>Descent of Noah from Ararat</i> (1889).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESarkssian196328_54-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESarkssian196328-54">[54]</a></sup> The unique <i>Valley of Mount Ararat</i> contains Aivazovksy's signature in Armenian: "Aivazian" (Ô±ÕµÕ¾Õ¡Õ¦Õ¥Õ¡Õ¶).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESarkssian196328_54-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESarkssian196328-54">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMikaelian199163_25-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMikaelian199163-25">[25]</a></sup> In a panorama of Venice expressed by <i>Byron's Visit to the Mekhitarists on St Lazarus Island in Venice</i> (1898); the foreground of the picture contains members of the Armenian Congregation giving an enthusiastic welcome to the poet.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECardwell2005402_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECardwell2005402-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<p>His other themed works from this period include rare portraits of notable Armenians, such as his brother Archbishop Gabriel Aivazovsky (<a href="/wiki/File:Gabriel_Aivazovsky.jpg" title="File:Gabriel Aivazovsky.jpg">1882</a>), Count <a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Loris-Melikov" title="Mikhail Loris-Melikov">Mikhail Loris-Melikov</a> (<a href="/wiki/File:LorisMelikov_Aivazovsky.jpg" title="File:LorisMelikov Aivazovsky.jpg">1888</a>), Catholicos <a href="/wiki/Mkrtich_Khrimian" title="Mkrtich Khrimian">Mkrtich Khrimian</a> (<a href="/wiki/File:Aivazovsky_-_Catholicos_Khrimyan_Airik_near_Echmiadzin.jpg" title="File:Aivazovsky - Catholicos Khrimyan Airik near Echmiadzin.jpg">1895</a>), <a href="/wiki/Nakhichevan-on-Don" title="Nakhichevan-on-Don">Nakhichevan-on-Don</a> Mayor Ðrutyun Khalabyan and others.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESarkssian196328_54-3"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESarkssian196328-54">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Khachatrian_23-10"><a href="#cite_note-Khachatrian-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<p><i>The Baptism of Armenians</i> and <i>Oath Before the Battle of Avarayr</i> (both 1892) depict the two single most memorable events of ancient Armenia: the <a href="/wiki/Christianization" title="Christianization">Christianization</a> of Armenia via baptism of King <a href="/wiki/Tiridates_III_of_Armenia" title="Tiridates III of Armenia">Tiridates III</a> (early 4th century), and the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Avarayr" title="Battle of Avarayr">Battle of Avarayr</a> of 451.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Khachatrian_23-11"><a href="#cite_note-Khachatrian-23">[23]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Influence">Influence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ivan_Aivazovsky&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Influence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Aivazovsky was the most influential seascape painter in nineteenth-century Russian art.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tretyakovgallery_17-7"><a href="#cite_note-tretyakovgallery-17">[17]</a></sup> According to the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Museum" title="Russian Museum">Russian Museum</a>, "he was the first and for a long time the only representative of seascape painting" and "all other artists who painted seascapes were either his own students or influenced by him."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rusmuseum.ru_51-1"><a href="#cite_note-rusmuseum.ru-51">[51]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Arkhip_Kuindzhi" title="Arkhip Kuindzhi">Arkhip Kuindzhi</a> (1841/2â1910) is cited by <a href="/wiki/Krugosvet" title="Krugosvet">Krugosvet</a> encyclopedia as having been influenced by Aivazovsky.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> In 1855, at age 13â14, Kuindzhi visited Feodosia to study with Aivazovsky, however, he was engaged merely to mix paints<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bowlt_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bowlt-59">[59]</a></sup> and instead studied with Adolf Fessler, Aivazovsky's student.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> A 1903 encyclopedic article stated: "Although Kuindzhi cannot be called a student of Aivazovsky, the latter had without doubt some influence on him in the first period of his activity; from whom he borrowed much in the manner of painting."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> English art historian <a href="/wiki/John_Ellis_Bowlt" title="John Ellis Bowlt">John E. Bowlt</a> wrote that "the elemental sense of light and form associated with Aivazovsky's sunsets, storms, and surging oceans permanently influenced the young Kuindzhi."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bowlt_59-1"><a href="#cite_note-Bowlt-59">[59]</a></sup></p>
<p>Aivazovsky also influenced Russian painters <a href="/wiki/Lev_Lagorio" title="Lev Lagorio">Lev Lagorio</a>, <a class="extiw" href="https://ru.wikipedia.org/wiki/%D0%9B%D0%B0%D1%82%D1%80%D0%B8,_%D0%9C%D0%B8%D1%85%D0%B0%D0%B8%D0%BB_%D0%9F%D0%B5%D0%BB%D0%BE%D0%BF%D0%B8%D0%B4%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B8%D1%87" title="ru:ÐÐ°ÑÑÐ¸, ÐÐ¸ÑÐ°Ð¸Ð» ÐÐµÐ»Ð¾Ð¿Ð¸Ð´Ð¾Ð²Ð¸Ñ">Mikhail Latri</a>, and <a class="extiw" href="https://ru.wikipedia.org/wiki/%D0%93%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%B7%D0%B5%D0%BD,_%D0%90%D0%BB%D0%B5%D0%BA%D1%81%D0%B5%D0%B9_%D0%92%D0%B0%D1%81%D0%B8%D0%BB%D1%8C%D0%B5%D0%B2%D0%B8%D1%87" title="ru:ÐÐ°Ð½Ð·ÐµÐ½, ÐÐ»ÐµÐºÑÐµÐ¹ ÐÐ°ÑÐ¸Ð»ÑÐµÐ²Ð¸Ñ">Aleksey Ganzen</a> (the latter two were his grandsons).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gomtsyan_26-1"><a href="#cite_note-Gomtsyan-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Recognition">Recognition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ivan_Aivazovsky&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Recognition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:279px;max-width:279px">
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:277px;max-width:277px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image"
