srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/%22%D0%A0%D1%83%D1%81%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D0%9C%D1%83%D0%B7%D0%B5%D0%B9%22%2C_%D0%BA%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%BD%D1%8B%D0%B9_%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BB%2C_%D0%B3.%D0%A1%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%BA%D1%82-%D0%9F%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B1%D1%83%D1%80%D0%B3.jpg/413px-%22%D0%A0%D1%83%D1%81%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D0%9C%D1%83%D0%B7%D0%B5%D0%B9%22%2C_%D0%BA%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%BD%D1%8B%D0%B9_%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BB%2C_%D0%B3.%D0%A1%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%BA%D1%82-%D0%9F%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B1%D1%83%D1%80%D0%B3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/%22%D0%A0%D1%83%D1%81%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D0%9C%D1%83%D0%B7%D0%B5%D0%B9%22%2C_%D0%BA%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%BD%D1%8B%D0%B9_%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BB%2C_%D0%B3.%D0%A1%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%BA%D1%82-%D0%9F%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B1%D1%83%D1%80%D0%B3.jpg/550px-%22%D0%A0%D1%83%D1%81%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D0%9C%D1%83%D0%B7%D0%B5%D0%B9%22%2C_%D0%BA%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%BD%D1%8B%D0%B9_%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BB%2C_%D0%B3.%D0%A1%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%BA%D1%82-%D0%9F%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B1%D1%83%D1%80%D0%B3.jpg 2x" width="275"/></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Several Aivazovsky paintings displayed <i>(left)</i> at the State <a href="/wiki/Russian_Museum" title="Russian Museum">Russian Museum</a> in Saint Petersburg.</div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:277px;max-width:277px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%D0%90%D0%B9%D0%B2%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%BE%D0%B2%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D0%98.%D0%9A._%D0%92%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%BD%D0%B0.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="2279" data-file-width="3957" height="158" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/%D0%90%D0%B9%D0%B2%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%BE%D0%B2%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D0%98.%D0%9A._%D0%92%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%BD%D0%B0.jpg/275px-%D0%90%D0%B9%D0%B2%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%BE%D0%B2%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D0%98.%D0%9A._%D0%92%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%BD%D0%B0.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/%D0%90%D0%B9%D0%B2%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%BE%D0%B2%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D0%98.%D0%9A._%D0%92%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%BD%D0%B0.jpg/413px-%D0%90%D0%B9%D0%B2%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%BE%D0%B2%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D0%98.%D0%9A._%D0%92%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%BD%D0%B0.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/%D0%90%D0%B9%D0%B2%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%BE%D0%B2%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D0%98.%D0%9A._%D0%92%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%BD%D0%B0.jpg/550px-%D0%90%D0%B9%D0%B2%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%BE%D0%B2%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D0%98.%D0%9A._%D0%92%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%BD%D0%B0.jpg 2x" width="275"/></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><i>Wave</i> (1889), one of the paintings exhibited</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Ivan Aivazovsky is one of the few Russian artists to achieve wide recognition during their lifetime.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tretyakovgallery_17-8"><a href="#cite_note-tretyakovgallery-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeek2012178_3-4"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeek2012178-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> Today, he is considered as one of the most prominent marine artists of the 19th century,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-artrenewal_39-2"><a href="#cite_note-artrenewal-39">[39]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> and, overall, one of the greatest marine artists in Russia and the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-paulfrasercollectibles_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-paulfrasercollectibles-65">[65]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rutgers_28-1"><a href="#cite_note-rutgers-28">[28]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> He was also one of the few Russian artists to become famous outside Russia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENewmarch1917193.E2.80.93194_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENewmarch1917193.E2.80.93194-71">[71]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> In 1898, <i><a href="/wiki/Munsey%27s_Magazine" title="Munsey's Magazine">Munsey's Magazine</a></i> wrote that Aivazovsky is "better known to the world at large than any other artist of his nationality, with the exception of the sensational <a href="/wiki/Vasily_Vereshchagin" title="Vasily Vereshchagin">Verestchagin</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> Although according to art historian Janet Whitmore he is relatively unknown in the west.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Whitmore_36-1"><a href="#cite_note-Whitmore-36">[36]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="In_Russia">In Russia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ivan_Aivazovsky&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: In Russia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1890, the <i><a href="/wiki/Brockhaus_and_Efron_Encyclopedic_Dictionary" title="Brockhaus and Efron Encyclopedic Dictionary">Brockhaus and Efron Encyclopedic Dictionary</a></i> described him as the "best Russian marine painter" (Ð»ÑÑÑÐ¸Ð¹ ÑÑÑÑÐºÐ¸Ð¹ Ð¼Ð°ÑÐ¸Ð½Ð¸ÑÑ).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ivan_Kramskoi" title="Ivan Kramskoi">Ivan Kramskoi</a>, one of the most prominent Russian artists of the nineteenth century, praised him thus: "Aivazovsky isâno matter who says whatâa star of first magnitude, and not only in our [country], but also in history of art in general."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-km.ru_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-km.ru-5">[5]</a></sup> Another Russian painter, Alexandre Benois, suggested that "Aivazovsky stands apart from the general history of the Russian school of landscape painting."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rusmuseum.ru_51-2"><a href="#cite_note-rusmuseum.ru-51">[51]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State_Russian_Museum" title="State Russian Museum">State Russian Museum</a> website continues, "It is hard to find another figure in the history of Russian art enjoying the same popularity among amateur viewers and erudite professionals alike."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rusmuseum.ru_51-3"><a href="#cite_note-rusmuseum.ru-51">[51]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Fyodor_Dostoyevsky" title="Fyodor Dostoyevsky">Fyodor Dostoyevsky</a>, a contemporary of Aivazovsky, wrote that his paintings are in great demand.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup></p>
<p>In nineteenth-century Russia, his name became a synonym for art and beauty. The phrase "worthy of Aivazovsky's brush" was the standard way of describing something ineffably lovely. It was first used by Anton Chekhov in his 1897 play <i><a href="/wiki/Uncle_Vanya" title="Uncle Vanya">Uncle Vanya</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chekhov_31-1"><a href="#cite_note-Chekhov-31">[31]</a></sup> In response to Marina Timofeevna's (the old nurse) query about the fight between Ivan Voynitsky ("Uncle Vanya") and Aleksandr Serebryakov, Ilya Telegin says that it was "A sight<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[a]</a></sup> worthy of Aivazovsky's brush" (Ð¡ÑÐ¶ÐµÑ, Ð´Ð¾ÑÑÐ¾Ð¹Ð½ÑÐ¹ ÐºÐ¸ÑÑÐ¸ ÐÐ¹Ð²Ð°Ð·Ð¾Ð²ÑÐºÐ¾Ð³Ð¾ <i>Syuzhet, dostoyniy kisti Ayvazovskovo</i>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[79]</a></sup></p>
<p>A street in <a href="/wiki/Moscow" title="Moscow">Moscow</a> (<a class="extiw" href="https://ru.wikipedia.org/wiki/%D0%A3%D0%BB%D0%B8%D1%86%D0%B0_%D0%90%D0%B9%D0%B2%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%BE%D0%B2%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B3%D0%BE_(%D0%9C%D0%BE%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B2%D0%B0)" title="ru:Ð£Ð»Ð¸ÑÐ° ÐÐ¹Ð²Ð°Ð·Ð¾Ð²ÑÐºÐ¾Ð³Ð¾ (ÐÐ¾ÑÐºÐ²Ð°)">ru</a>) was named after Aivazovsky in 1978.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[80]</a></sup> His first and only statue in Russia was erected in 2007 in <a href="/wiki/Kronstadt" title="Kronstadt">Kronstadt</a>, near Saint Petersburg.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[81]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="In_Armenia">In Armenia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ivan_Aivazovsky&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: In Armenia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%D5%80%D5%B8%D5%BE%D5%B0%D5%A1%D5%B6%D5%B6%D5%A5%D5%BD_%D4%B1%D5%B5%D5%BE%D5%A1%D5%A6%D5%B8%D5%BE%D5%BD%D5%AF%D5%AB_1.jpg"><img alt="The statue of Aivazovsky in Yerevan, Armenia" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="720" data-file-width="540" height="267" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/%D5%80%D5%B8%D5%BE%D5%B0%D5%A1%D5%B6%D5%B6%D5%A5%D5%BD_%D4%B1%D5%B5%D5%BE%D5%A1%D5%A6%D5%B8%D5%BE%D5%BD%D5%AF%D5%AB_1.jpg/200px-%D5%80%D5%B8%D5%BE%D5%B0%D5%A1%D5%B6%D5%B6%D5%A5%D5%BD_%D4%B1%D5%B5%D5%BE%D5%A1%D5%A6%D5%B8%D5%BE%D5%BD%D5%AF%D5%AB_1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/%D5%80%D5%B8%D5%BE%D5%B0%D5%A1%D5%B6%D5%B6%D5%A5%D5%BD_%D4%B1%D5%B5%D5%BE%D5%A1%D5%A6%D5%B8%D5%BE%D5%BD%D5%AF%D5%AB_1.jpg/300px-%D5%80%D5%B8%D5%BE%D5%B0%D5%A1%D5%B6%D5%B6%D5%A5%D5%BD_%D4%B1%D5%B5%D5%BE%D5%A1%D5%A6%D5%B8%D5%BE%D5%BD%D5%AF%D5%AB_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/%D5%80%D5%B8%D5%BE%D5%B0%D5%A1%D5%B6%D5%B6%D5%A5%D5%BD_%D4%B1%D5%B5%D5%BE%D5%A1%D5%A6%D5%B8%D5%BE%D5%BD%D5%AF%D5%AB_1.jpg/400px-%D5%80%D5%B8%D5%BE%D5%B0%D5%A1%D5%B6%D5%B6%D5%A5%D5%BD_%D4%B1%D5%B5%D5%BE%D5%A1%D5%A6%D5%B8%D5%BE%D5%BD%D5%AF%D5%AB_1.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%D5%80%D5%B8%D5%BE%D5%B0%D5%A1%D5%B6%D5%B6%D5%A5%D5%BD_%D4%B1%D5%B5%D5%BE%D5%A1%D5%A6%D5%B8%D5%BE%D5%BD%D5%AF%D5%AB_1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The statue of Aivazovsky in central <a href="/wiki/Yerevan" title="Yerevan">Yerevan</a>, Armenia, erected in 2003.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[82]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[83]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Aivazovsky has always been considered an Armenian painter in his ancestral homeland<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Khachatrian_23-12"><a href="#cite_note-Khachatrian-23">[23]</a></sup> and virtually always referred to there by his original Armenian name, Hovhannes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[84]</a></sup> Virtually all Armenian, some Russian<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[85]</a></sup> and English<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lang_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-Lang-4">[4]</a></sup> sources, refer to him as Hovhannes Ayvazovski (<a href="/wiki/Armenian_language" title="Armenian language">Armenian</a>: <span lang="hy">ÕÕ¸Õ¾Õ°Õ¡Õ¶Õ¶Õ¥Õ½ Ô±ÕµÕ¾Õ¡Õ¦Õ¸Õ¾Õ½Õ¯Õ«</span>; <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a>: <span lang="ru">ÐÐ²Ð°Ð½(Ð½)ÐµÑ ÐÐ¹Ð²Ð°Ð·Ð¾Ð²ÑÐºÐ¸Ð¹ <i>Ovan(n)es Aivazovsky</i></span>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-km.ru_5-2"><a href="#cite_note-km.ru-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[86]</a></sup> The artist signed some of his paintings and letters in <a href="/wiki/Armenian_alphabet" title="Armenian alphabet">Armenian</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAdamian195889_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAdamian195889-88">[87]</a></sup> For instance, his signatures in both Armenian (Ô±ÕµÕ¾Õ¡Õ¦Õ¥Õ¡Õ¶, <i>Ayvazean</i>) and Russian (ÐÐ¹Ð²Ð°Ð·Ð¾Ð²ÑÐºÑÐ¹, <i>Ayvazovskiy</i>) appear on <i>Valley of Mount Ararat</i> (1882).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarutiunian196593_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarutiunian196593-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p>Aivazovsky has been described as the "most remarkable" Armenian painter of the 19th century and the first-ever Armenian marine painter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lang_4-2"><a href="#cite_note-Lang-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESarkissian196770_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESarkissian196770-89">[88]</a></sup> He was born outside Armenia proper, and like his contemporaries, including <a href="/wiki/Gevorg_Bashinjaghian" title="Gevorg Bashinjaghian">Gevorg Bashinjaghian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Panos_Terlemezian" title="Panos Terlemezian">Panos Terlemezian</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Vardges_Sureniants" title="Vardges Sureniants">Vardges Sureniants</a>, Aivazovsky lived outside his homeland, drawing primary influences from European and Russian schools of art. His creativity and viewpoint have been attributed to his uniquely Armenian roots. According to Sureniants, he sought to create a union which would have brought together all Armenian artists around the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Khachatrian_23-13"><a href="#cite_note-Khachatrian-23">[23]</a></sup> The prominent Armenian poet <a href="/wiki/Hovhannes_Tumanyan" title="Hovhannes Tumanyan">Hovhannes Tumanyan</a> wrote a short poem titled "In Front of an Aiazovsky painting" (Â«Ô±ÕµÕ¾Õ¡Õ¦Õ¸Õ¾Õ½Õ¯Õ¸Ö Õ¶Õ¯Õ¡ÖÕ« Õ¡Õ¼Õ»ÖÂ») in 1893. It is inspired by painting of the sea by Aivazovsky, mostly likely from the 1870sâ1890s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[89]</a></sup> It was translated into English in 1917 by <a href="/wiki/Alice_Stone_Blackwell" title="Alice Stone Blackwell">Alice Stone Blackwell</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[90]</a></sup></p>
<p>Several paintings of Aivazovsky from the National Gallery of Armenia hang in the <a href="/wiki/Presidential_Palace,_Yerevan" title="Presidential Palace, Yerevan">Presidential Palace</a> in Yerevan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[91]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Elsewhere">Elsewhere</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ivan_Aivazovsky&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Elsewhere">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In Ukraine, he is sometimes considered a Ukrainian painter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[92]</a></sup> He was included in a 2001 book titled <i>100 Greatest Ukrainians</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[93]</a></sup> An alley in <a href="/wiki/Kiev" title="Kiev">Kiev</a> (<a class="extiw" href="https://uk.wikipedia.org/wiki/%D0%9F%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B2%D1%83%D0%BB%D0%BE%D0%BA_%D0%90%D0%B9%D0%B2%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%BE%D0%B2%D1%81%D1%8C%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B3%D0%BE_(%D0%9A%D0%B8%D1%97%D0%B2)" title="uk:ÐÑÐ¾Ð²ÑÐ»Ð¾Ðº ÐÐ¹Ð²Ð°Ð·Ð¾Ð²ÑÑÐºÐ¾Ð³Ð¾ (ÐÐ¸ÑÐ²)">ÐÑÐ¾Ð²ÑÐ»Ð¾Ðº ÐÐ¹Ð²Ð°Ð·Ð¾Ð²ÑÑÐºÐ¾Ð³Ð¾</a>) was named after him in 1939. A three-star hotel in <a href="/wiki/Odessa" title="Odessa">Odessa</a>, where dozens of his works are displayed, is named for him as well.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[94]</a></sup> A statue of Aivazovsky and his brother Gabriel is located in Simferopol, Crimea's administrative center.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[95]</a></sup></p>
<p>Aivazovsky's painting were popular in the Ottoman imperial court during the 19th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[96]</a></sup> According to <i><a href="/wiki/H%C3%BCrriyet_Daily_News" title="HÃ¼rriyet Daily News">HÃ¼rriyet Daily News</a></i>, as of 2014, 30 paintings of Aivazovsky are on display in museums in Turkey.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[97]</a></sup> According to another source, there are 41 paintings of Aivazovsky on display in Turkey, 21 in former palaces of Ottoman sultans, 10 in various marine and military museums, and 10 at the presidential residence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sputnik_turkey_99-0"><a href="#cite_note-sputnik_turkey-99">[98]</a></sup> In 2007, when <a href="/wiki/Abdullah_G%C3%BCl" title="Abdullah GÃ¼l">Abdullah GÃ¼l</a> became president of Turkey, he brought paintings by Aivazovsky up from the basement to hang in his office during redecoration of the presidential palace, the <a href="/wiki/%C3%87ankaya_Mansion" title="Ãankaya Mansion">Ãankaya Mansion</a> in Ankara.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[99]</a></sup> Pictures of official meetings of <a href="/wiki/Recep_Tayyip_Erdo%C4%9Fan" title="Recep Tayyip ErdoÄan">Recep Tayyip ErdoÄan</a> at the new <a href="/wiki/Presidential_Complex" title="Presidential Complex">Presidential Complex</a> in Ankara show that the walls of the rooms at the presidential residence are decorated with Aivazovsky's artwork.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sputnik_turkey_99-1"><a href="#cite_note-sputnik_turkey-99">[98]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legacy">Legacy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ivan_Aivazovsky&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Legacy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%D0%A4%D0%B5%D0%BE%D0%B4%D0%BE%D1%81%D0%B8%D1%8F._%D0%9F%D0%B0%D0%BC%27%D1%8F%D1%82%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BA_%D0%86._%D0%9A._%D0%90%D0%B9%D0%B2%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%BE%D0%B2%D1%81%D1%8C%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%BC%D1%83..JPG"><img alt="Aivazovsky's sculpture monument in front of his house Aivazovsky National Art Gallery" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1443" data-file-width="904" height="271" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/%D0%A4%D0%B5%D0%BE%D0%B4%D0%BE%D1%81%D0%B8%D1%8F._%D0%9F%D0%B0%D0%BC%27%D1%8F%D1%82%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BA_%D0%86._%D0%9A._%D0%90%D0%B9%D0%B2%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%BE%D0%B2%D1%81%D1%8C%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%BC%D1%83..JPG/170px-%D0%A4%D0%B5%D0%BE%D0%B4%D0%BE%D1%81%D0%B8%D1%8F._%D0%9F%D0%B0%D0%BC%27%D1%8F%D1%82%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BA_%D0%86._%D0%9A._%D0%90%D0%B9%D0%B2%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%BE%D0%B2%D1%81%D1%8C%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%BC%D1%83..JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/%D0%A4%D0%B5%D0%BE%D0%B4%D0%BE%D1%81%D0%B8%D1%8F._%D0%9F%D0%B0%D0%BC%27%D1%8F%D1%82%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BA_%D0%86._%D0%9A._%D0%90%D0%B9%D0%B2%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%BE%D0%B2%D1%81%D1%8C%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%BC%D1%83..JPG/255px-%D0%A4%D0%B5%D0%BE%D0%B4%D0%BE%D1%81%D0%B8%D1%8F._%D0%9F%D0%B0%D0%BC%27%D1%8F%D1%82%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BA_%D0%86._%D0%9A._%D0%90%D0%B9%D0%B2%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%BE%D0%B2%D1%81%D1%8C%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%BC%D1%83..JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/%D0%A4%D0%B5%D0%BE%D0%B4%D0%BE%D1%81%D0%B8%D1%8F._%D0%9F%D0%B0%D0%BC%27%D1%8F%D1%82%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BA_%D0%86._%D0%9A._%D0%90%D0%B9%D0%B2%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%BE%D0%B2%D1%81%D1%8C%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%BC%D1%83..JPG/340px-%D0%A4%D0%B5%D0%BE%D0%B4%D0%BE%D1%81%D0%B8%D1%8F._%D0%9F%D0%B0%D0%BC%27%D1%8F%D1%82%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BA_%D0%86._%D0%9A._%D0%90%D0%B9%D0%B2%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%BE%D0%B2%D1%81%D1%8C%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%BC%D1%83..JPG 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%D0%A4%D0%B5%D0%BE%D0%B4%D0%BE%D1%81%D0%B8%D1%8F._%D0%9F%D0%B0%D0%BC%27%D1%8F%D1%82%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BA_%D0%86._%D0%9A._%D0%90%D0%B9%D0%B2%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%BE%D0%B2%D1%81%D1%8C%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%BC%D1%83..JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Aivazovsky's monument in front of his house (<a href="/wiki/Aivazovsky_National_Art_Gallery" title="Aivazovsky National Art Gallery">now an art gallery</a>) in Feodosia</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Aivazovsky's house in Feodosia, where he had founded an art museum in 1880, is open to this day as the <a href="/wiki/Aivazovsky_National_Art_Gallery" title="Aivazovsky National Art Gallery">Aivazovsky National Art Gallery</a>. It remains a central attraction in the city<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Whitmore_36-2"><a href="#cite_note-Whitmore-36">[36]</a></sup> and holds the world's largest collections (417) of Aivazovsky paintings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Obukhovska_30-3"><a href="#cite_note-Obukhovska-30">[30]</a></sup> A statue of the artist is erected in front of the it.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Posthumous_honors">Posthumous honors</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ivan_Aivazovsky&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Posthumous honors">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> (1950),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[100]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Republic_of_Romania" title="Socialist Republic of Romania">Romania</a> (1971),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ukrweekly_102-0"><a href="#cite_note-ukrweekly-102">[101]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[102]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Madagascar" title="Madagascar">Madagascar</a> (1988),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[103]</a></sup> Armenia (first in 1992),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[104]</a></sup> Russia (1995),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[105]</a></sup> Ukraine (1999),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[106]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Abkhazia" title="Abkhazia">Abkhazia</a> (1999),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[107]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Moldova" title="Moldova">Moldova</a> (2010),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[108]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Kyrgyzstan" title="Kyrgyzstan">Kyrgyzstan</a> (2010),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[109]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Burundi" title="Burundi">Burundi</a> (2012),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[110]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Mozambique" title="Mozambique">Mozambique</a> (2013)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[111]</a></sup> have issued postage stamps depicting Aivazovsky or his works.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ukrweekly_102-1"><a href="#cite_note-ukrweekly-102">[101]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Minor_planet" title="Minor planet">minor planet</a> <a href="/wiki/3787_Aivazovskij" title="3787 Aivazovskij">3787 Aivazovskij</a>, named after Aivazovsky, was discovered by Soviet astronomer <a href="/wiki/Nikolai_Chernykh" title="Nikolai Chernykh">Nikolai Chernykh</a> in 1977.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[112]</a></sup></p>
<p>An exhibition featuring 120 paintings and 55 etchings of Aivazovsky was held at the <a href="/wiki/Tretyakov_Gallery" title="Tretyakov Gallery">Tretyakov Gallery on Krymsky Val</a> from July 29 to November 20, 2016 dedicated to his 200th anniversary of birth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[113]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[114]</a></sup> In the first 2 weeks, the exhibition had around 55,000 visitors, a record number.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[115]</a></sup> 38 of the works were moved from the Aivazovsky Art Gallery in Feodosia, which prompted Ukraine to call for an international boycott of the Tretyakov Gallery as it considers Crimea an occupied territory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[116]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Auctions">Auctions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ivan_Aivazovsky&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Auctions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Aivazovsky's paintings began appearing in auctions (mostly in London) in the early 2000s. Many of his works are being bought by <a href="/wiki/Russian_oligarch" title="Russian oligarch">Russian oligarchs</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[117]</a></sup></p>
<p>His works have risen steadily in auction value.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[118]</a></sup> In 2004, his <i><a href="/wiki/Saint_Isaac%27s_Cathedral" title="Saint Isaac's Cathedral">Saint Isaac's Cathedral</a> On A Frosty Day</i>, a rare cityscape, sold for around Â£1 million ($1.9 million).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[119]</a></sup> In 2007, his painting <i>American Shipping off the Rock of Gibraltar</i> auctioned at Â£2.71 million, "more than four times its top estimate". It was, "the highest price paid at auction for Aivazovsky" at the time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[120]</a></sup> In April 2012, his 1856 work <i><a href="/wiki/File:Aivazovsky_-_View_of_Constantinople_and_the_Bosphorus.jpg" title="File:Aivazovsky - View of Constantinople and the Bosphorus.jpg">View of Constantinople and the Bosphorus</a></i> was sold at <a href="/wiki/Sotheby%27s" title="Sotheby's">Sotheby's</a> for a record $5.2 million (Â£3.2 million),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[121]</a></sup> a tenfold increase since it was last at an auction in 1995.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[122]</a></sup></p>
<p>In June 2015 Sotheby's withdrew from auction an 1870 Aivazovsky painting <i>Evening in Cairo</i>, which was estimated at Â£1.5â2 million ($2â$3 million), after the Russian Interior Ministry claimed that it was stolen in 1997 from a private collection in Moscow.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[123]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[124]</a></sup></p>
